1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

If MCP search returns no results:

# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.


## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of the findings:

## Kafka Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern

The lifecycle is implemented across these key files in `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489`:

### Core Interface
- **`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala`** — The `Server` trait (Startable/Stoppable equivalent) defining `startup()`, `shutdown()`, `awaitShutdown()`, plus `ProcessStatus` states (SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN)
- **`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaBroker.scala`** — Broker-specific lifecycle trait

### Implementations
- **`KafkaRaftServer`** — Orchestrates startup/shutdown ordering: **controller first, broker last** on startup; **broker first, controller last** on shutdown (reverse order)
- **`BrokerServer`** — Implements `KafkaBroker`, performs controlled shutdown (waits for partition leadership transfer)
- **`ControllerServer`** — Implements the controller process lifecycle
- **`BrokerLifecycleManager`** — State machine managing registration, heartbeats, and coordinated shutdown
- **`SharedServer`** — Shared Raft/metadata components with reference-counting start/stop

### Worker Thread Lifecycle
- **`ShutdownableThread`** (`server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java`) — Abstract Java base class with `initiateShutdown()` + `awaitShutdown()` pattern used throughout the codebase

### Entry Point
- **`kafka.Kafka`** — Registers a JVM shutdown hook, calls `startup()`, blocks on `awaitShutdown()`

],\n  \"text\": \"Kafka's service initialization lifecycle is built around a small set of core abstractions in the sg-evals/kafka--0753c489 repository:\\n\\n1. **`Server` trait** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala`): The top-level lifecycle interface defining `startup()`, `shutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()`. Also defines the `ProcessStatus` sealed trait with states SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, and SHUTTING_DOWN used by implementors to guard concurrent state transitions.\\n\\n2. **`KafkaBroker` trait** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaBroker.scala`): Broker-specific lifecycle interface extending Logging, exposing `startup()`, `shutdown(timeout: Duration)`, `awaitShutdown()`, and `isShutdown()` along with accessors for all broker subsystems.\\n\\n3. **`KafkaRaftServer`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaRaftServer.scala`): The concrete `Server` implementation for KRaft mode. Implements the coordinated startup ordering: **controller starts first** (so it is ready to handle broker registration), then broker. For shutdown, **broker shuts down first** (to perform controlled shutdown with the controller), then controller\u2014reverse startup order.\\n\\n4. **`BrokerServer`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala`): Implements `KafkaBroker`. Uses `maybeChangeStatus()` with `ProcessStatus` to prevent concurrent lifecycle transitions. During shutdown, calls `replicaManager.beginControlledShutdown()` and `lifecycleManager.beginControlledShutdown()`, waits for the controller to confirm partition leadership transfer, then tears down subsystems in reverse startup order.\\n\\n5. **`ControllerServer`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ControllerServer.scala`): Implements the controller process lifecycle with the same `maybeChangeStatus()` state machine pattern.\\n\\n6. **`BrokerLifecycleManager`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerLifecycleManager.scala`): Owns the broker state machine (registering, fenced, active, controlled shutdown). Manages broker registration with the controller (KIP-631) and periodic heartbeats. Exposes `beginShutdown()` and `beginControlledShutdown()` to coordinate graceful shutdown. Uses an event queue for sequential state transitions.\\n\\n7. **`SharedServer`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/SharedServer.scala`): Manages components shared between BrokerServer and ControllerServer in combined mode (Raft manager, metadata loader, snapshot generator). Implements reference-style start/stop via `startForBroker`/`startForController` and `stopForBroker`/`stopForController`\u2014shared resources are only stopped when neither server needs them.\\n\\n8. **`ShutdownableThread`** (`server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java`): The foundational abstract Java class for all Kafka worker threads. Provides `initiateShutdown()` (signals the thread via CountDownLatch and optional interrupt), `awaitShutdown()` (blocks until the thread exits), and `shutdown()` (combines both). Subclasses implement `doWork()` called in a loop until shutdown is initiated.\\n\\n9. **`Scheduler` interface / `KafkaScheduler`** (`server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java`, `KafkaScheduler.java`): A task scheduler service with `startup()` and `shutdown()` lifecycle methods used throughout the broker for periodic background tasks.\\n\\n10. **`RaftManager` / `KafkaRaftManager`** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/raft/RaftManager.scala`): The Raft consensus layer with `startup()` and `shutdown()` lifecycle methods, started and stopped by SharedServer.\\n\\n11. **`Kafka` object** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/Kafka.scala`): The main entry point. Builds a `KafkaRaftServer`, registers a JVM shutdown hook via `Exit.addShutdownHook` that calls `server.shutdown()` on SIGTERM/SIGINT, calls `server.startup()`, then blocks on `server.awaitShutdown()`.\\n\\nThe key design pattern is reverse-order shutdown: components that start last are stopped first, ensuring that dependent services (broker) stop before their dependencies (controller, Raft layer, shared infrastructure). The `BrokerLifecycleManager` adds a coordinated controlled-shutdown phase where the broker notifies the controller to transfer partition leadership before stopping, minimizing disruption to producers and consumers.\"\n}\n",
